  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[File:Michael I 2014 Romanian stamp 2.jpg|thumb|Michael and Anne on a 2014 Romanian stamp]]&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;[[File:Michael I 2014 Romanian stamp 2.jpg|thumb|Michael and Anne on a 2014 Romanian stamp]]&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;After their wedding in 1948, Anne and Michael rented a house in [[Hertfordshire]] for four years, where they became market gardeners and farmed poultry. In 1956 they moved to [[Versoix]] on [[Lake Geneva]], and raised five daughters there.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; In 1992, they visited Romania for three days; it was her first visit to the country.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; That same year, Anne celebrated her 69th birthday when her mother, Margaret, died one day after her 97th.&lt;/del&gt; From 1993 to 1997, despite repeated attempts, Michael was refused entry to Romania by [[Văcăroiu I Cabinet|the hostile Romanian government]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; During these years Anne visited the country a number of times representing her husband. After 1997, there were no restrictions on Anne and Michael's entry into Romania. [[Elisabeta Palace]] was put at their disposal by the government, and they recovered some properties from the state, including [[Săvârşin Castle]] and [[Peleş Castle]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;erhj&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;After their wedding in 1948, Anne and Michael rented a house in [[Hertfordshire]] for four years, where they became market gardeners and farmed poultry. In 1956 they moved to [[Versoix]] on [[Lake Geneva]], and raised five daughters there.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; In 1992, they visited Romania for three days; it was her first visit to the country.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; From 1993 to 1997, despite repeated attempts, Michael was refused entry to Romania by [[Văcăroiu I Cabinet|the hostile Romanian government]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; During these years Anne visited the country a number of times representing her husband. After 1997, there were no restrictions on Anne and Michael's entry into Romania. [[Elisabeta Palace]] was put at their disposal by the government, and they recovered some properties from the state, including [[Săvârşin Castle]] and [[Peleş Castle]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;erhj&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;

After 1997, there were no restrictions on Anne and Michael's entry into Romania. [[Elisabeta Palace]] was put at their disposal by the government, and they recovered some properties from the state, including [[Săvârşin Castle]] and [[Peleş Castle]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;erhj&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;After their wedding in 1948, Anne and Michael rented a house in [[Hertfordshire]] for four years, where they became market gardeners and farmed poultry. In 1956 they moved to [[Versoix]] on [[Lake Geneva]], and raised five daughters there.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; In 1992, they visited Romania for three days; it was her first visit to the country.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; From 1993 to 1997, despite repeated attempts, Michael was refused entry to Romania by [[Văcăroiu I Cabinet|the hostile Romanian government]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;:0&quot; /&amp;gt; During these years Anne visited the country a number of times representing her husband. After 1997, there were no restrictions on Anne and Michael's entry into Romania. [[Elisabeta Palace]] was put at their disposal by the government, and they recovered some properties from the state, including [[Săvârşin Castle]] and [[Peleş Castle]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;erhj&quot; /&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In June 2008, Anne and Michael celebrated their [[Anniversary gifts|diamond wedding]] anniversary with three days of events in Romania, which was the largest celebration the couple ever had since their wedding in June 1948.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.familiaregala.ro/stiri/articol/aniversarea-casatoriei-majestatilor-lor |title=Aniversarea căsătoriei Majestăților Lor |website=Familiaregala.ro |access-date=9 March 2016}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In June 2008, Anne and Michael celebrated their [[Anniversary gifts|diamond wedding]] anniversary with three days of events in Romania, which was the largest celebration the couple ever had since their wedding in June 1948.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.familiaregala.ro/stiri/articol/aniversarea-casatoriei-majestatilor-lor |title=Aniversarea căsătoriei Majestăților Lor |website=Familiaregala.ro |access-date=9 March 2016}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

However, the use of the term ''saint'' depends on the context and [[Christian denomination|denomination]]. In [[Catholic Church|Catholic]], [[Eastern Orthodox Church|Eastern Orthodox]], [[Anglican Communion|Anglican]], [[Oriental Orthodox]], and [[Lutheranism|Lutheran]] doctrine, all of their faithful deceased in Heaven are considered to be saints, but some are considered worthy of greater honor or emulation.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Woodward1996&quot;&amp;gt;{{cite book|last=Woodward|first=Kenneth L.|authorlink=Kenneth L. Woodward|title=Making Saints|date=1996|publisher=Simon &amp;amp; Sachier&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

However, the use of the term ''saint'' depends on the context and [[Christian denomination|denomination]]. In [[Catholic Church|Catholic]], [[Eastern Orthodox Church|Eastern Orthodox]], [[Anglican Communion|Anglican]], [[Oriental Orthodox]], and [[Lutheranism|Lutheran]] doctrine, all of their faithful deceased in Heaven are considered to be saints, but some are considered worthy of greater honor or emulation.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Woodward1996&quot;&amp;gt;{{cite book|last=Woodward|first=Kenneth L.|authorlink=Kenneth L. Woodward|title=Making Saints|date=1996|publisher=Simon &amp;amp; Sachier&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

On rare occasions, new names (usually monks or bishops) are grafted onto their traditional list of saints.... Something like the cult continues among Anglicans and Lutherans, who maintain feast days and calendars of saints. But while the Anglicans have no mechanism for recognizing new saints, the Lutherans from time to time do informally recommend new names (Da Hammarskjold, Dietrick Bonhoeffer, and Pope John XXIII are recent additions) for thanksgiving and remembrance by the faithful. The saint, then, is a familiar figure in all world religions. But only the Roman Catholic Church has a formal, continuous, and highly rationalized process for 'making' saints.}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Official ecclesiastical recognition, and consequently a public cult of [[veneration]], is conferred on some denominational saints through the process of [[canonization]] in the Catholic Church or [[glorification]] in the Eastern Orthodox Church after their approval.&amp;lt;ref name=bebis&amp;gt;{{cite web&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

On rare occasions, new names (usually monks or bishops) are grafted onto their traditional list of saints.... Something like the cult continues among Anglicans and Lutherans, who maintain feast days and calendars of saints. But while the Anglicans have no mechanism for recognizing new saints, the Lutherans from time to time do informally recommend new names (Da Hammarskjold, Dietrick Bonhoeffer, and Pope John XXIII are recent additions) for thanksgiving and remembrance by the faithful. The saint, then, is a familiar figure in all world religions. But only the Roman Catholic Church has a formal, continuous, and highly rationalized process for 'making' saints.}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Official ecclesiastical recognition, and consequently a public cult of [[veneration]], is conferred on some denominational saints through the process of [[canonization]] in the Catholic Church or [[glorification]] in the Eastern Orthodox Church after their approval.&amp;lt;ref name=bebis&amp;gt;{{cite web&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In October 2022, the [[&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Leader&lt;/del&gt; of the &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Conservative&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Party (UK)&lt;/del&gt;|&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Conservative&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Party leader&lt;/del&gt;]] and [[&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Prime Minister&lt;/del&gt; of the &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;United&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Kingdom&lt;/del&gt;|&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Prime&lt;/del&gt; &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Minister&lt;/del&gt;]] [[Liz Truss]] announced that she was to resign,&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;bbc-resigns&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=20 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss resigns: PM's exit kicks off another Tory leadership race |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-63332037 |access-date=20 October 2022 |archive-date=20 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221020124108/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-63332037 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; following pressure from Conservative MPs citing the loss in public confidence in the government's policies following the [[September 2022 United Kingdom mini-budget|September 2022 mini-budget]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;truss-quit-ft&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=17 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss battles for survival as City figures and MPs call on her to quit |work=Financial Times |url=https://www.ft.com/content/38b30b44-94c2-4775-8efb-2c95b3e8c447 |access-date=17 October 2022 |archive-date=16 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221016220844/https://www.ft.com/content/38b30b44-94c2-4775-8efb-2c95b3e8c447 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Truss announced her resignation on 20 October, 44 days after taking office. Her resignation was to take effect [[October 2022 Conservative Party leadership election (UK)|once her successor is elected by the party]], anticipated to happen by the following week.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;bbc-resigns&quot;/&amp;gt; This would make her [[List of prime ministers of the United Kingdom by length of tenure|shortest tenured prime minister]] in the United Kingdom's history.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=20 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss resigns as prime minister |language=en-GB |work=Sky News |url=https://news.sky.com/story/liz-truss-to-resign-as-prime-minister-sky-news-understands-12723236 |access-date=20 October 2022 |archive-date=20 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221020124052/https://news.sky.com/story/liz-truss-to-resign-as-prime-minister-sky-news-understands-12723236 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In October 2022, the&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; British&lt;/ins&gt; [[&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Prime Minister&lt;/ins&gt; of the &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;United&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Kingdom&lt;/ins&gt;|&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Prime&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Minister&lt;/ins&gt;]] and&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; the&lt;/ins&gt; [[&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Leader&lt;/ins&gt; of the &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Conservative&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Party (UK)&lt;/ins&gt;|&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Conservative&lt;/ins&gt; &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Party leader&lt;/ins&gt;]]&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;,&lt;/ins&gt; [[Liz Truss]]&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;,&lt;/ins&gt; announced that she was to resign,&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;bbc-resigns&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=20 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss resigns: PM's exit kicks off another Tory leadership race |work=BBC News |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-63332037 |access-date=20 October 2022 |archive-date=20 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221020124108/https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-politics-63332037 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; following pressure from Conservative MPs citing the loss in public confidence in the government's policies following the [[September 2022 United Kingdom mini-budget|September 2022 mini-budget]].&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;truss-quit-ft&quot;&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=17 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss battles for survival as City figures and MPs call on her to quit |work=Financial Times |url=https://www.ft.com/content/38b30b44-94c2-4775-8efb-2c95b3e8c447 |access-date=17 October 2022 |archive-date=16 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221016220844/https://www.ft.com/content/38b30b44-94c2-4775-8efb-2c95b3e8c447 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Truss announced her resignation on 20 October, 44 days after taking office. Her resignation was to take effect [[October 2022 Conservative Party leadership election (UK)|once her successor is elected by the party]], anticipated to happen by the following week.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;bbc-resigns&quot;/&amp;gt; This would make her [[List of prime ministers of the United Kingdom by length of tenure|shortest tenured prime minister]] in the United Kingdom's history.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite news |date=20 October 2022 |title=Liz Truss resigns as prime minister |language=en-GB |work=Sky News |url=https://news.sky.com/story/liz-truss-to-resign-as-prime-minister-sky-news-understands-12723236 |access-date=20 October 2022 |archive-date=20 October 2022 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221020124052/https://news.sky.com/story/liz-truss-to-resign-as-prime-minister-sky-news-understands-12723236 |url-status=live }}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diffot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In religious belief, a '''&lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;saint&lt;/del&gt;''' is a person who is recognized as having an exceptional degree of [[Q-D-Š|holiness]], likeness, or closeness to [[God]]. However, the use of the term ''saint'' depends on the context and [[Christian denomination|denomination]]. In [[Catholic Church|Catholic]], [[Eastern Orthodox Church|Eastern Orthodox]], [[Anglican Communion|Anglican]], [[Oriental Orthodox]], and [[Lutheranism|Lutheran]] doctrine, all of their faithful deceased in Heaven are considered to be saints, but some are considered worthy of greater honor or emulation.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Woodward1996&quot;&amp;gt;{{cite book|last=Woodward|first=Kenneth L.|authorlink=Kenneth L. Woodward|title=Making Saints|date=1996|publisher=Simon &amp;amp; Sachier&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

However, the use of the term ''saint'' depends on the context and [[Christian denomination|denomination]]. In [[Catholic Church|Catholic]], [[Eastern Orthodox Church|Eastern Orthodox]], [[Anglican Communion|Anglican]], [[Oriental Orthodox]], and [[Lutheranism|Lutheran]] doctrine, all of their faithful deceased in Heaven are considered to be saints, but some are considered worthy of greater honor or emulation.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Woodward1996&quot;&amp;gt;{{cite book|last=Woodward|first=Kenneth L.|authorlink=Kenneth L.   &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;|quote=Among other Christian churches, the Russian Orthodox retains a vigorous devotion to the saints, especially the early church fathers and martyrs. On rare occasions, new names (usually monks or bishops) are grafted onto their traditional list of saints.... Something like the cult continues among Anglicans and Lutherans, who maintain feast days and calendars of saints. But while the Anglicans have no mechanism for recognizing new saints, the Lutherans from time to time do informally recommend new names (Da Hammarskjold, Dietrick Bonhoeffer, and Pope John XXIII are recent additions) for thanksgiving and remembrance by the faithful. The saint, then, is a familiar figure in all world religions. But only the Roman Catholic Church has a formal, continuous, and highly rationalized process for 'making' saints.}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Official ecclesiastical recognition, and consequently a public cult of [[veneration]], is conferred on some denominational saints through the process of [[canonization]] in the Catholic Church or [[glorification]] in the Eastern Orthodox Church after their approval.&amp;lt;ref name=bebis&amp;gt;{{cite web&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

On rare occasions, new names (usually monks or bishops) are grafted onto their traditional list of saints.... Something like the cult continues among Anglicans and Lutherans, who maintain feast days and calendars of saints. But while the Anglicans have no mechanism for recognizing new saints, the Lutherans from time to time do informally recommend new names (Da Hammarskjold, Dietrick Bonhoeffer, and Pope John XXIII are recent additions) for thanksgiving and remembrance by the faithful. The saint, then, is a familiar figure in all world religions. But only the Roman Catholic Church has a formal, continuous, and highly rationalized process for 'making' saints.}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Official ecclesiastical recognition, and consequently a public cult of [[veneration]], is conferred on some denominational saints through the process of [[canonization]] in the Catholic Church or [[glorification]] in the Eastern Orthodox Church after their approval.&amp;lt;ref name=bebis&amp;gt;{{cite web&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

Viitorul finished 9 points ahead of the main contender, [[FC Gloria Buzău|Gloria Buzău]]. However, a [[Romanian Football Federation]] inquiry proved that Viitorul did not have three youth teams in the county-level competition, as required by Liga III regulations, and gave Viitorul a 9-point penalty that led Gloria Buzău finishing first.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite web|url=https://liga2.prosport.ro/liga-3/stiri/promovarea-viitorului-axintele-inca-o-enigma-10959180|title=Promovarea Viitorului Axintele, încă o enigmă|trans-title=Promotion of Viitorul Axintele, another enigma|accessdate=19 October 2022|publisher=liga2.prosport.ro|archive-date=19 October 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20221019182149/https://liga2.prosport.ro/liga-3/stiri/promovarea-viitorului-axintele-inca-o-enigma-10959180|url-status=live}}{{in lang|ro}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite web|url=https://www.guraialomitei.com/stiri/viitorul-axintele-si-rapid-fetesti-au-fost-depunctate/|title=Viitorul Axintele și Rapid Fetești au fost depunctate|trans-title=Viitorul Axintele and Rapid Fetești were deducted|accessdate=19 October 2022|publisher=guraialomitei.com|archive-date=3 August 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210803021138/https://www.guraialomitei.com/stiri/viitorul-axintele-si-rapid-fetesti-au-fost-depunctate/|url-status=live}}{{in lang|ro}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://frf.ro/sectiune/comunicate-frf/articol/decizii-ale-comisiei-disciplina-frf-0|title=Decizii ale comisiei de disciplină a FRF|trans-title=Decisions of the disciplinary committee of the FRF|access-date=14 June 2013|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130618064000/http://frf.ro/sectiune/comunicate-frf/articol/decizii-ale-comisiei-disciplina-frf-0|url-status=dead|archive-date=18 June 2013|df=mdy-all}}{{in lang|ro}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

		<id>https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wilder_Brigade_Monument&amp;diff=1117233537&amp;oldid=1117137668</id>
		<title>Wilder Brigade Monument</title>
		<link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Wilder_Brigade_Monument&amp;diff=1117233537&amp;oldid=1117137668"/>

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;&lt;span dir=&quot;auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;autocomment&quot;&gt;Background: &lt;/span&gt;assume gender&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;table style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122;&quot; data-mw=&quot;interface&quot;&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-content&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-content&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;tr class=&quot;diff-title&quot; lang=&quot;en&quot;&gt;
				&lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;&quot;&gt;← Previous revision&lt;/td&gt;
				&lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Revision as of 16:27, 20 October 2022&lt;/td&gt;
				&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 27:&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 27:&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In mid-1863, during the [[American Civil War]], the [[Army of the Cumberland]] ([[Union Army]]) was conducting a [[military campaign]] targeting the city of [[Chattanooga, Tennessee]]. By September of that year, the [[Army of Tennessee]] ([[Confederate States Army]]) had withdrawn from [[Tennessee]] and into [[north Georgia]], near [[Lafayette, Georgia]]. Starting on September 18, the two armies fought in the [[Battle of Chickamauga]], which lasted until September 20 and was one of the bloodiest battles in the war, with approximately 35,000 soldiers killed, wounded, captured, or missing.{{sfn|National Park Service}} During the battle, Union officer [[John T. Wilder]] led his [[brigade]] (known as the [[Lightning Brigade]]) into action.{{sfn|Smith|2009|p=100}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In mid-1863, during the [[American Civil War]], the [[Army of the Cumberland]] ([[Union Army]]) was conducting a [[military campaign]] targeting the city of [[Chattanooga, Tennessee]]. By September of that year, the [[Army of Tennessee]] ([[Confederate States Army]]) had withdrawn from [[Tennessee]] and into [[north Georgia]], near [[Lafayette, Georgia]]. Starting on September 18, the two armies fought in the [[Battle of Chickamauga]], which lasted until September 20 and was one of the bloodiest battles in the war, with approximately 35,000 soldiers killed, wounded, captured, or missing.{{sfn|National Park Service}} During the battle, Union officer [[John T. Wilder]] led his [[brigade]] (known as the [[Lightning Brigade]]) into action.{{sfn|Smith|2009|p=100}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Several years later, in August 1890, several former officers from the brigade met to discuss a brigade reunion. At that time, the idea of a [[monument]] honoring the brigade at the Chickamauga battlefield was brought up. Wilder approved of the idea and promised to match whatever funds were raised by the brigade, with the plan to have each [[regiment]] contribute $1,000 and the [[Artillery battery|battery]] contribute $500. The monument would be the first one erected on the battlefield. In August 1891, a monument organization was created at the reunion, and fundraising commenced. Fundraising was initially successful, and in early 1892, construction of the monument began. However, by 1893, fundraising had slowed, and the financial situation was worsened by a [[bank failure]] at a Tennessee bank holding $1,200 for the organization. As a result, work stopped, with the monument only partially constructed. In 1895, another reunion held at the battlefield led to additional money being raised, but not enough to restart construction. In 1897, [[Indianapolis]] &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;businessperson&lt;/del&gt; Arthur McKain donated $1,200 to Wilder to help fund the monument, and construction resumed shortly afterward.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}} While initial monument designs were drawn up by Harry Hargraves,{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=8}} they had undergone significant revisions, and by the time construction restarted, E. E. Betts had modified the design. By 1898, Wilder stated that the monument would be dedicated the following year.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Several years later, in August 1890, several former officers from the brigade met to discuss a brigade reunion. At that time, the idea of a [[monument]] honoring the brigade at the Chickamauga battlefield was brought up. Wilder approved of the idea and promised to match whatever funds were raised by the brigade, with the plan to have each [[regiment]] contribute $1,000 and the [[Artillery battery|battery]] contribute $500. The monument would be the first one erected on the battlefield. In August 1891, a monument organization was created at the reunion, and fundraising commenced. Fundraising was initially successful, and in early 1892, construction of the monument began. However, by 1893, fundraising had slowed, and the financial situation was worsened by a [[bank failure]] at a Tennessee bank holding $1,200 for the organization. As a result, work stopped, with the monument only partially constructed. In 1895, another reunion held at the battlefield led to additional money being raised, but not enough to restart construction. In 1897, [[Indianapolis]] &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;businessman&lt;/ins&gt; Arthur McKain donated $1,200 to Wilder to help fund the monument, and construction resumed shortly afterward.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}} While initial monument designs were drawn up by Harry Hargraves,{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=8}} they had undergone significant revisions, and by the time construction restarted, E. E. Betts had modified the design. By 1898, Wilder stated that the monument would be dedicated the following year.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;=== Dedication and later history ===&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;&lt;span dir=&quot;auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;autocomment&quot;&gt;Background: &lt;/span&gt;assume gender&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In mid-1863, during the [[American Civil War]], the [[Army of the Cumberland]] ([[Union Army]]) was conducting a [[military campaign]] targeting the city of [[Chattanooga, Tennessee]]. By September of that year, the [[Army of Tennessee]] ([[Confederate States Army]]) had withdrawn from [[Tennessee]] and into [[north Georgia]], near [[Lafayette, Georgia]]. Starting on September 18, the two armies fought in the [[Battle of Chickamauga]], which lasted until September 20 and was one of the bloodiest battles in the war, with approximately 35,000 soldiers killed, wounded, captured, or missing.{{sfn|National Park Service}} During the battle, Union officer [[John T. Wilder]] led his [[brigade]] (known as the [[Lightning Brigade]]) into action.{{sfn|Smith|2009|p=100}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In mid-1863, during the [[American Civil War]], the [[Army of the Cumberland]] ([[Union Army]]) was conducting a [[military campaign]] targeting the city of [[Chattanooga, Tennessee]]. By September of that year, the [[Army of Tennessee]] ([[Confederate States Army]]) had withdrawn from [[Tennessee]] and into [[north Georgia]], near [[Lafayette, Georgia]]. Starting on September 18, the two armies fought in the [[Battle of Chickamauga]], which lasted until September 20 and was one of the bloodiest battles in the war, with approximately 35,000 soldiers killed, wounded, captured, or missing.{{sfn|National Park Service}} During the battle, Union officer [[John T. Wilder]] led his [[brigade]] (known as the [[Lightning Brigade]]) into action.{{sfn|Smith|2009|p=100}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;

At that time, the idea of a [[monument]] honoring the brigade at the Chickamauga battlefield was brought up. Wilder approved of the idea and promised to match whatever funds were raised by the brigade, with the plan to have each [[regiment]] contribute $1,000 and the [[Artillery battery|battery]] contribute $500. The monument would be the first one erected on the battlefield. In August 1891, a monument organization was created at the reunion, and fundraising commenced. Fundraising was initially successful, and in early 1892, construction of the monument began. However, by 1893, fundraising had slowed, and the financial situation was worsened by a [[bank failure]] at a Tennessee bank holding $1,200 for the organization. As a result, work stopped, with the monument only partially constructed. In 1895, another reunion held at the battlefield led to additional money being raised, but not enough to restart construction. In 1897, [[Indianapolis]] &lt;del style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;businessperson&lt;/del&gt; Arthur McKain donated $1,200 to Wilder to help fund the monument, and construction resumed shortly afterward.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}} While initial monument designs were drawn up by Harry Hargraves,{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=8}} they had undergone significant revisions, and by the time construction restarted, E. E. Betts had modified the design. By 1898, Wilder stated that the monument would be dedicated the following year.{{sfn|''Dedication of the Wilder Brigade Monument''|1900|p=6}}&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

	<entry>
		<id>https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vistage_Worldwide,_Inc.&amp;diff=1117233523&amp;oldid=0</id>
		<title>Vistage Worldwide, Inc.</title>
		<link rel="alternate" type="text/html" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Vistage_Worldwide,_Inc.&amp;diff=1117233523&amp;oldid=0"/>
		<updated>2022-10-20T16:27:53Z</updated>

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=&quot;/w/index.php?title=User:Jxmxpx96&amp;amp;action=edit&amp;amp;redlink=1&quot; class=&quot;new mw-userlink&quot; title=&quot;User:Jxmxpx96 (page does not exist)&quot;&gt;&lt;bdi&gt;Jxmxpx96&lt;/bdi&gt;&lt;/a&gt; moved page &lt;a href=&quot;/w/index.php?title=Vistage_Worldwide,_Inc.&amp;amp;redirect=no&quot; class=&quot;mw-redirect&quot; title=&quot;Vistage Worldwide, Inc.&quot;&gt;Vistage Worldwide, Inc.&lt;/a&gt; to &lt;a href=&quot;/wiki/Vistage_Worldwide,_Inc&quot; title=&quot;Vistage Worldwide, Inc&quot;&gt;Vistage Worldwide, Inc&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;New page&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div&gt;'''Vistage Worldwide''' is a [[peer mentoring]] membership organization for [[CEO]]s, business owners and executives of small- to mid-size businesses. Founded in 1957 as ''The Executive Committee'', Vistage has more than 28,000 members in 26 countries. The Vistage model offers three key components: guidance from an executive mentor (called a Vistage Chair), participation in a peer advisory group made up of 12-16 CEOs or business owners, and access to thought leadership, including subject matter experts and a library of business articles and resources. &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite web|url=https://www.consultancy.uk/news/16665/ceo-advisory-community-vistage-buys-uks-academy-for-chief-executives|title=CEO advisory community Vistage buys UK's Academy for Chief Executives|website=www.consultancy.uk|language=en|access-date=2018-09-01}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{Cite news|url=https://www.towerbrook.com/portfolio/vistage/|title=VISTAGE|work=TowerBrook|access-date=2018-09-01|language=en-US}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.sdbj.com/services/vistage-gives-leaders-useful-perspective-and-peer/ &amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Through the MyVistage online network, Vistage members are also connected with tens of thousands of other CEOs and top executives around the world, giving them 24/7 access to feedback, input, resources and solutions.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
Sam Reese was named Vistage CEO in 2016. &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.sdbj.com/uncategorized/sam-reese-appointed-ceo-vistage-worldwide-inc/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; In 2022, Vistage’s management team partnered with Gridiron Capital to acquire Vistage from Providence Equity Partners. &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://gridironcapital.com/vistage-partners-with-gridiron-capital-to-accelerate-growth-and-expansion-worldwide/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
==History==&lt;br /&gt;
The company was founded in 1957 by a Wisconsin businessman named Robert Nourse.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.vistage.com/about-vistage/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Nourse thought it would be beneficial if company presidents and CEOs came together to talk about their challenges and seek guidance from one another. It was the beginning of what would become widely known as an executive peer advisory group, forum or “board.”  From the start, Nourse brought together business leaders from similarly sized companies in non-competing industries. Conversations were candid and confidential. The purpose was to get fresh perspectives, think through problems and to learn from one another. The meetings became increasingly popular, prompting Nourse to turn the model into a business, called The Executive Committee (TEC), which later became Vistage Worldwide (although a few locations still operate under the TEC name).&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
TEC had three core elements: the peer group (made up of CEOs and small business owners),  the facilitator (known as a “Chair”) and a speaker (resource specialist or subject matter expert). Nourse expanded TEC by creating additional groups in other locations. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
==About Vistage CEO peer advisory groups==&lt;br /&gt;
The hallmarks of a classic Vistage CEO peer advisory group is that it is confidential, consists of 12-16 business leaders (peers) from non-competing companies; is made up of member businesses across all industries; and is a safe forum for working out issues and exploring opportunities. There are hundreds of such groups across the country and around the world. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
==Locations==&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage Worldwide, Inc. is based in San Diego, California and has a UK base in Southampton, UK. Vistage is also active in Argentina, Australia, Brazil, Canada, China, Chile, Columbia, Germany, Ireland, Malaysia, Malta, Mexico, the Netherlands, New Zealand, Paraguay, Peru, Portugal, Singapore, Israel, South Africa, Spain, the United Kingdom, United Arab Emirates, Gibraltar and Uruguay. &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.vistage.com/about-vistage/vistage-locations/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
==Timeline==&lt;br /&gt;
===1958-1977===&lt;br /&gt;
Milwaukee-area executives from non-competing industries were getting together to share their challenges, opportunities and goals. The conversations were candid. The meetings were confidential. When the group had more questions than answers, Founder Bob Nourse brought in experts to share their perspectives. CEOs started to see results and Nourse saw the need for expansion. Soon, TEC groups were forming outside of Wisconsin.&lt;br /&gt;
In 1968, CEO coaches (also known as Vistage Chairs) Fred Chaney and Bill Hall launched TEC California with TEC 7 (now CE-7).&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===1978===&lt;br /&gt;
By 1978, TEC had grown to 245 members in 23 groups. The company moved its headquarters from Wisconsin to Southern California.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===1986===&lt;br /&gt;
Dr. W. Lynn Tanner brought the peer advisory model to Canada. Tanner, a former executive for Pan Am Airlines, attended a TEC meeting in the U.S. as a guest and immediately recognized the power of the peer advisory format. Tanner’s TEC Canada became the company’s first international licensee.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
TEC Australia was also founded.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===1988===&lt;br /&gt;
TEC reaches 1,000 members&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===1989-96===&lt;br /&gt;
TEC continues its international expansion, founding TEC United Kingdom, TEC Asia and TEC Brazil.&lt;br /&gt;
 &lt;br /&gt;
In 1991, Chaney and Hall purchased a license to expand TEC nationwide, creating the company that would eventually become Vistage. The duo also entered into licensing agreements to establish TEC in other countries.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2003===&lt;br /&gt;
The CEO Confidence Index &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.vistage.com/research-center/vistage-ceo-survey/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; launches, a quarterly report based on the sentiment of SMB CEOs about the economy, their hiring and investment plans, and prospects for their revenues and profitability. This index is frequently referenced by media outlets including Inc &amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.inc.com/joe-galvin/dont-let-high-costs-eat-your-companys-profits-try-these-4-solutions.html&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; and the New York Times&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.nytimes.com/2018/07/06/business/economy/jobs-report.html&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;. Today it is called the Vistage CEO Confidence Index.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2004===&lt;br /&gt;
After steady growth for 45+ years, TEC reaches 10,000 members worldwide in 12 countries.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2006===&lt;br /&gt;
TEC (The Executive Committee) changed its name to Vistage Worldwide, however, not all of the company’s licensees adopted the new name. Currently the company operates under the name &amp;quot;Vistage&amp;quot;, (a portmanteau of vista and advantage) with several of its licensees operating under the name TEC.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2012===&lt;br /&gt;
TowerBrook Capital Partners and Education Growth Partners acquire majority interest in Vistage Worldwide.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.sdbj.com/finance/towerbrook-capital-acquires-majority-interest-vist/&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage begins a monthly survey of its members in collaboration with the WSJ&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.wsj.com/articles/we-are-at-the-limit-trumps-tariffs-turn-small-businesses-upside-down-1533660467?mod=hp_lead_pos5 {{Bare URL inline|date=October 2022}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;, called the Wall Street Journal/Vistage Small Business CEO Survey&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10000872396390444358804578018372546832136 {{Bare URL inline|date=October 2022}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;.  The survey reveals insights on the sentiment of U.S. CEOs and small-business owners from a broad range of industries. Respondents represent a random sampling of Vistage members.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage acquires TEC Midwest in Michigan.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;https://www.biztimes.com/2016/industries/banking-finance/tec-midwest-sold-to-vistage-worldwide/&amp;amp;sa=D&amp;amp;source=docs&amp;amp;ust=1666212856044558&amp;amp;usg=AOvVaw3VPhyACjUTLf6CXRVS2NIX&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2018===&lt;br /&gt;
Providence Equity Partners Acquires Vistage.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage launches the Emerging Leader program. Guided by a Vistage Chair, this 2-year program helps first-line managers and high-impact individual contributors develop the leadership skills needed to deliver on company goals.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2020===&lt;br /&gt;
A Dun &amp;amp; Bradstreet analysis found that in 2020 Vistage member companies grew their revenue by 4.6%, while similar nonmember companies saw revenue decrease by 4.7%.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
===2022===&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage has  28,000+ members in 26 countries.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
Vistage’s management team partners with Gridiron Capital to acquire Vistage from Providence Equity Partners. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
A full suite of Vistage leadership development programs are launched to help CEOs cultivate their staff members and retain top talent at all levels of the company.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;
==References==&lt;br /&gt;
&amp;lt;references /&amp;gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;br /&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;A student desk can be any desk form meant for use by an enrollee in elementary, secondary or postsecondary education. Anna Breadin designed and patented a one-piece school desk in the late 1880s that was built with a table section attached in front of a wooden seat and back rest. Before this, most students in America sat either on chairs or long benches at long tables.&amp;lt;ref name=interior&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.linuxhow.in/articles/home-family/interior-design/a-short-history-of-school-desks/|title=A Short History of Desks|publisher=Interior Design|access-date=2012-05-17|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://archive.is/20120804114909/http://www.linuxhow.in/articles/home-family/interior-design/a-short-history-of-school-desks/|archive-date=2012-08-04}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;A student desk can be any desk form meant for use by an enrollee in elementary, secondary or postsecondary education. Anna Breadin designed and patented a one-piece school desk in the late 1880s that was built with a table section attached in front of a wooden seat and back rest. Before this, most students in America sat either on chairs or long benches at long tables.&amp;lt;ref name=interior&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=http://www.linuxhow.in/articles/home-family/interior-design/a-short-history-of-school-desks/|title=A Short History of Desks|publisher=Interior Design|access-date=2012-05-17|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://archive.is/20120804114909/http://www.linuxhow.in/articles/home-family/interior-design/a-short-history-of-school-desks/|archive-date=2012-08-04}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;==Notable examples==&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;*The [[Resolute desk|''Resolute'' desk]] in the [[Oval Office]] has been used by many [[United States]] presidents, including [[John F. Kennedy]], [[Ronald Reagan]] and [[Barack Obama]]. It is made from the timbers of {{HMS|Resolute|1850|6}}, an abandoned British ship discovered by an American vessel and returned to [[Queen Victoria|Queen Victoria of Great Britain]] as a token of friendship and goodwill. Queen Victoria commissioned the desk from William Evenden, Royal Naval Dockyard at Chatham, England, and presented it to President [[Rutherford B. Hayes]] in 1880.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web| url= http://www.whitehousemuseum.org/furnishings/resolute-desk.htm |title=Resolute desk |publisher= The White House Museum |access-date=2012-05-17}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;*&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; &lt;/ins&gt;The [[Resolute desk|''Resolute'' desk]] in the [[Oval Office]] has been used by many [[United States]] presidents, including [[John F. Kennedy]], [[Ronald Reagan]] and [[Barack Obama]]. It is made from the timbers of {{HMS|Resolute|1850|6}}, an abandoned British ship discovered by an American vessel and returned to [[Queen Victoria|Queen Victoria of Great Britain]] as a token of friendship and goodwill. Queen Victoria commissioned the desk from William Evenden, Royal Naval Dockyard at Chatham, England, and presented it to President [[Rutherford B. Hayes]] in 1880.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web| url= http://www.whitehousemuseum.org/furnishings/resolute-desk.htm |title=Resolute desk |publisher= The White House Museum |access-date=2012-05-17}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a name=&quot;movedpara_4_0_rhs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;*&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; &lt;/ins&gt;The [[Bureau du Roi]] ({{IPA-fr|byʁo dy ʁwa}}, ''the King's desk''), also known as Louis XV's roll-top secretary ({{lang-fr|Secrétaire à cylindre de Louis XV}}), is the richly ornamented royal [[cylinder desk]] which was constructed at the end of [[Louis XV of France|Louis XV]]'s reign, and is now again in the [[Palace of Versailles]].&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-empty diff-side-deleted&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;a class=&quot;mw-diff-movedpara-right&quot; title=&quot;Paragraph was moved. Click to jump to old location.&quot; href=&quot;#movedpara_8_1_lhs&quot;&gt;&amp;#x26AB;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a name=&quot;movedpara_6_0_rhs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;*&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; &lt;/ins&gt;[[Henry VIII's writing desk]] is a portable [[writing desk]], made in about 1525-26 for [[Henry VIII of England|Henry VIII]]. It is currently in the [[Victoria and Albert Museum]].  The desk is a product of the royal workshops and is lavishly embellished with ornamental motifs introduced to the [[Kingdom of England]] by continental artists.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;&lt;a name=&quot;movedpara_8_1_lhs&quot;&gt;&lt;/a&gt;*[[Henry VIII's writing desk]] is a portable [[writing desk]], made in about 1525-26 for [[Henry VIII of England|Henry VIII]]. ''The Other Guys'' is the only one not to be co-written by Ferrell. It is also the first of three collaborations between Ferrell and Wahlberg, who later reunited in ''[[Daddy's Home (film)|Daddy's Home]]'' (2015) and ''[[Daddy's Home 2]]'' (2017).&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

''The Other Guys'' is the only one not to be co-written by Ferrell. It is also the first of three collaborations between Ferrell and Wahlberg, who later reunited in ''[[Daddy's Home (film)|Daddy's Home]]'' (2015) and ''[[Daddy's Home 2]]'' (2017).&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;&lt;span dir=&quot;auto&quot;&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;autocomment&quot;&gt;Death: &lt;/span&gt; ce&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;table style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122;&quot; data-mw=&quot;interface&quot;&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; /&gt;

  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 122:&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 122:&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In April 1997, Pasquale &quot;Fat Pat&quot; Musitano, the boss of the Musitano family, met with Gaetano &quot;Guy&quot; Panepinto, the Toronto agent of Montreal's Rizzuto family, in Niagara Falls.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=284}} Musitano was unhappy with the way that his family was subordinate to the Papalia family, which in turn was the Canadian branch of the Magaddino family.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=283-284}} Both Papalia and his right-hand man Barillaro were &quot;made men&quot; in the Magaddino family, and Musitano needed the &quot;protection&quot; of a more powerful family to avoid retaliation from the Buffalo family should either be killed. Musitano wanted an alignment with the Rizzuto family, which in turn was looking to expand into Ontario.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=283-284}}    &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;In April 1997, Pasquale &quot;Fat Pat&quot; Musitano, the boss of the Musitano family, met with Gaetano &quot;Guy&quot; Panepinto, the Toronto agent of Montreal's Rizzuto family, in Niagara Falls.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=284}} Musitano was unhappy with the way that his family was subordinate to the Papalia family, which in turn was the Canadian branch of the Magaddino family.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=283-284}} Both Papalia and his right-hand man Barillaro were &quot;made men&quot; in the Magaddino family, and Musitano needed the &quot;protection&quot; of a more powerful family to avoid retaliation from the Buffalo family should either be killed. Musitano wanted an alignment with the Rizzuto family, which in turn was looking to expand into Ontario.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=283-284}}    &lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Papalia was fatally shot in the head on May 31, 1997, at the age of 73 in the parking lot of 20 Railway Street outside his vending machine business, Galaxy Vending, in Hamilton.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite news|url=https://www.thespec.com/news/hamilton-region/2016/09/23/may-31-1997-mob-boss-johnny-pops-papalia-executed-in-hamilton.html|title=May 31, 1997: Mob boss Johnny (Pops) Papalia executed in Hamilton|newspaper=The Hamilton Spectator|publisher=thespec.com|date=September 23, 2016|access-date=July 11, 2020|archive-date=January 7, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210107044408/https://www.thespec.com/news/hamilton-region/2016/09/23/may-31-1997-mob-boss-johnny-pops-papalia-executed-in-hamilton.html|url-status=live}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[hitman]] [[Kenneth Murdock]] claimed that he had been ordered to kill Papalia by Angelo and Pat Musitano of the [[Musitano crime family]] who owed $250,000 in [[bookmaking]] debts to Papalia.&amp;lt;ref name=kill&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com/news/ontario/2010/08/13/mafia_hitman_reveals_his_code_for_killings.html|title=Mafia hitman reveals his code for killings|work=thestar.com|date=August 13, 2010|access-date=December 8, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220075937/https://www.thestar.com/news/ontario/2010/08/13/mafia_hitman_reveals_his_code_for_killings.html|archive-date=December 20, 2016|url-status=live}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[hitman]] [[Kenneth Murdock]] claimed that he had been ordered to kill Papalia by Angelo and Pat Musitano of the [[Musitano crime family]] who owed $250,000 in [[bookmaking]] debts to Papalia.&amp;lt;ref name=kill&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=https://www.thestar.com/news/ontario/2010/08/13/mafia_hitman_reveals_his_code_for_killings.html|title=Mafia hitman reveals his code for killings|work=thestar.com|date=August 13, 2010|access-date=December 8, 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161220075937/https://www.thestar.com/news/ontario/2010/08/13/mafia_hitman_reveals_his_code_for_killings.html|archive-date=December 20, 2016|url-status=live}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; the &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;Musitanos&lt;/ins&gt;.{{sfn|Cédilot|Noël|2012|p=282}} &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;After&lt;/ins&gt;   &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;'''Shohimardon''' (also ''Shakhimardan'', {{lang-uz|Shohimardon / Шоҳимардон}},&amp;lt;ref name=ome/&amp;gt; {{lang-ru|Шахимардан|Shakhimardan}}) is a village in [[Fergana District]] of [[Fergana Region]] in eastern [[Uzbekistan]].&amp;lt;ref name=class&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=https://stat.uz/uploads/docs/soato(mhobt)_2020.xlsx|title=Classification system of territorial units of the Republic of Uzbekistan|language=uz, ru|date=July 2020|publisher=The State Committee of the Republic of Uzbekistan on statistics}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; It is an [[exclave]] of Uzbekistan, surrounded by [[Kyrgyzstan]], in a valley in the [[Pamiro-Alai]] mountains. The river [[Shohimardonsoy]] flows through the village.&amp;lt;ref name=ome&amp;gt;{{cite encyclopedia|url=https://n.ziyouz.com/books/uzbekiston_milliy_ensiklopediyasi/O'zbekiston%20Milliy%20Ensiklopediyasi%20-%20Sh%20harfi.pdf|title=Шоҳимардонсой|trans-title=Shohimardonsoy|encyclopedia=[[National Encyclopedia of Uzbekistan]]|page=215|language=uz|year=2000–2005|location=Tashkent}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;'''Shohimardon''' (also ''Shakhimardan'', {{lang-uz|Shohimardon / Шоҳимардон}},&amp;lt;ref name=ome/&amp;gt; {{lang-ru|Шахимардан|Shakhimardan}}) is a village in [[Fergana District]] of [[Fergana Region]] in eastern [[Uzbekistan]].&amp;lt;ref name=class&amp;gt;{{cite web|url=https://stat.uz/uploads/docs/soato(mhobt)_2020.xlsx|title=Classification system of territorial units of the Republic of Uzbekistan|language=uz, ru|date=July 2020|publisher=The State Committee of the Republic of Uzbekistan on statistics}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; It is an [[exclave]] of Uzbekistan, surrounded by [[Kyrgyzstan]], in a valley in the [[Pamiro-Alai]] mountains. The river [[Shohimardonsoy]] flows through the village.&amp;lt;ref name=ome&amp;gt;{{cite encyclopedia|url=https://n.ziyouz.com/books/uzbekiston_milliy_ensiklopediyasi/O'zbekiston%20Milliy%20Ensiklopediyasi%20-%20Sh%20harfi.pdf|title=Шоҳимардонсой|trans-title=Shohimardonsoy|encyclopedia=[[National Encyclopedia of Uzbekistan]]|page=215|language=uz|year=2000–2005|location=Tashkent}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

		<title>Tourism in India</title>

		<summary type="html">&lt;p&gt;Tourist Guide in India&lt;/p&gt;
&lt;table style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122;&quot; data-mw=&quot;interface&quot;&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-content&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;col class=&quot;diff-content&quot; /&gt;
				&lt;tr class=&quot;diff-title&quot; lang=&quot;en&quot;&gt;
				&lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;&quot;&gt;← Previous revision&lt;/td&gt;
				&lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; style=&quot;background-color: #fff; color: #202122; text-align: center;&quot;&gt;Revision as of 16:27, 20 October 2022&lt;/td&gt;
				&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 29:&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td colspan=&quot;2&quot; class=&quot;diff-lineno&quot;&gt;Line 29:&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;The [[World Economic Forum]]'s ''[[Travel and Tourism Development Index]]'' 2021, which replaced its previous ''[[Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report]],'' ranks India 54th out of 117 countries overall.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web |title=Travel &amp;amp; Tourism Development Index 2021 Rebuilding for a Sustainable and Resilient Future |url=https://www3.weforum.org/docs/WEF_Travel_Tourism_Development_2021.pdf |website=weforum.org |publisher=World Economic Forum |access-date=24 June 2022 |page=13 |date=May 2022}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The last edition of the ''Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report'', published in 2019, had ranked India 34th out of 140 countries overall. The report ranked the price competitiveness of India's tourism sector 13th out of 140 countries. It mentioned that India has quite good air transport infrastructure (ranked 33rd), particularly given the country's stage of development, and reasonable ground and port infrastructure (ranked 28th). The country also scored high on natural resources (ranked 14th), and cultural resources and business travel (ranked 8th).&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web |title=Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report 2019 |url=http://www3.weforum.org/docs/WEF_TTCR_2019.pdf|website=weforum.org |access-date=10 September 2019}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[World Tourism Organization]] reported that India's receipts from tourism during 2012 ranked 16th in the world, and 7th among [[Asia-Pacific|Asian and Pacific]] countries.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite press release |url=http://pib.nic.in/newsite/PrintRelease.aspx?relid=103255 |title=Rank in Tourism |publisher=Press Information Bureau, Government of India |date=7 February 2014 |access-date=8 February 2014}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;The [[World Economic Forum]]'s ''[[Travel and Tourism Development Index]]'' 2021, which replaced its previous ''[[Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report]],'' ranks India 54th out of 117 countries overall.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web |title=Travel &amp;amp; Tourism Development Index 2021 Rebuilding for a Sustainable and Resilient Future |url=https://www3.weforum.org/docs/WEF_Travel_Tourism_Development_2021.pdf |website=weforum.org |publisher=World Economic Forum |access-date=24 June 2022 |page=13 |date=May 2022}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The last edition of the ''Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report'', published in 2019, had ranked India 34th out of 140 countries overall. The report ranked the price competitiveness of India's tourism sector 13th out of 140 countries. It mentioned that India has quite good air transport infrastructure (ranked 33rd), particularly given the country's stage of development, and reasonable ground and port infrastructure (ranked 28th). The country also scored high on natural resources (ranked 14th), and cultural resources and business travel (ranked 8th).&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite web |title=Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report 2019 |url=http://www3.weforum.org/docs/WEF_TTCR_2019.pdf|website=weforum.org |access-date=10 September 2019}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; The [[World Tourism Organization]] reported that India's receipts from tourism during 2012 ranked 16th in the world, and 7th among [[Asia-Pacific|Asian and Pacific]] countries.&amp;lt;ref&amp;gt;{{cite press release |url=http://pib.nic.in/newsite/PrintRelease.aspx?relid=103255 |title=Rank in Tourism |publisher=Press Information Bureau, Government of India |date=7 February 2014 |access-date=8 February 2014}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;
&lt;tr&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;The [[Ministry of Tourism (India)|Ministry of Tourism]] designs national policies for the development and promotion of tourism. In the process, the Ministry consults and collaborates with other stakeholders in the sector including various [[Union Government ministries of India|central ministries]]/[[List of Union Government agencies of India|agencies]], [[State governments of India|state governments]], union territories and private sector representatives. Concerted efforts are being made to promote niche tourism products such as rural, cruise, medical and eco-tourism.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport2017–18&quot; /&amp;gt; The Ministry of Tourism maintains the [[Incredible India]] campaign focused on promoting tourism in India.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;The [[Ministry of Tourism (India)|Ministry of Tourism]] designs national policies for the development and promotion of tourism. In the process, the Ministry consults and collaborates with other stakeholders in the sector including various [[Union Government ministries of India|central ministries]]/[[List of Union Government agencies of India|agencies]], [[State governments of India|state governments]], union territories and private sector representatives. Concerted efforts are being made to promote niche tourism products such as rural, cruise, medical and eco-tourism.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;AnnualReport2017–18&quot; /&amp;gt; The Ministry of Tourism maintains the [[Incredible India]] campaign focused on promoting tourism in India.&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt; incredible India [https://gowithharry.com/best-tourist-guide-in-india/ Tourist Guides] are the Ambassador's of Tourism in India&lt;/ins&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
&lt;/tr&gt;

  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;−&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #ffe49c; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Crook and Duval's Division marched beyond the Second Woods (on north side of Red Bud Run), and faced south. At 3:00{{nbsp}}pm they charged across the creek supported by du Pont's guns.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Wert84&quot;/&amp;gt; The Confederates responded with the brigade of Colonel Edmund N. Atkinson and Lieutenant Colonel Carter M. Braxton's guns.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt; Hayes' First Brigade went after Braxton only to discover that this end of Red Bud Run was swampy and difficult to cross. Hayes and the 23rd Ohio Infantry were able to get to the other side, but other regiments sought better places to ford the creek.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt; Braxton moved his artillery before Hayes could get out of the mud, and the commander of Duval's Second Brigade, Colonel [[Daniel D. Johnson]], was seriously wounded near the edge of the swamp. Adding to Duval's problems, Patton's Brigade left Lee's cavalry and deployed behind a stone wall to assist Atkinson.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td class=&quot;diff-marker&quot; data-marker=&quot;+&quot;&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
  &lt;td style=&quot;color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #a3d3ff; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Crook and Duval's Division marched beyond the Second Woods (on north side of Red Bud Run), and faced south. At 3:00{{nbsp}}pm they charged across the creek supported by du Pont's guns.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Wert84&quot;/&amp;gt; The Confederates responded with the brigade of Colonel Edmund N. Atkinson and Lieutenant Colonel &lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;[[Carter Moore Braxton|&lt;/ins&gt;Carter M. Braxton's&lt;ins style=&quot;font-weight: bold; text-decoration: none;&quot;&gt;]]&lt;/ins&gt; guns.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt; Hayes' First Brigade went after Braxton only to discover that this end of Red Bud Run was swampy and difficult to cross. Hayes and the 23rd Ohio Infantry were able to get to the other side, but other regiments sought better places to ford the creek.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt; Braxton moved his artillery before Hayes could get out of the mud, and the commander of Duval's Second Brigade, Colonel [[Daniel D. Johnson]], was seriously wounded near the edge of the swamp. Adding to Duval's problems, Patton's Brigade left Lee's cavalry and deployed behind a stone wall to assist Atkinson.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;

  &lt;td style=&quot;background-color: #f8f9fa; color: #202122; font-size: 88%; border-style: solid; border-width: 1px 1px 1px 4px; border-radius: 0.33em; border-color: #eaecf0; vertical-align: top; white-space: pre-wrap;&quot;&gt;&lt;div&gt;Thoburn's 1st Division heard the noise from Duval's charge and made a charge of their own from the First Woods westward along the south side of Red Bud Run.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;Ainsworth1902p368&quot;&amp;gt;{{harvnb|Ainsworth|Kirkley|1902|p=368}}&amp;lt;/ref&amp;gt; Near the center of the Middle Field, it received volleys from Gordon's Division and from Battle's Brigade of Rodes' Division. Battle's Brigade was now under command of Colonel Samuel B. Pickens, since Battle had assumed command of the division after Rodes' death.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt; The portion of Atkinson's Brigade that had turned to face Duval received enfilading fire from Thoburn. Confronted on two sides, Atkinson's Brigade began falling back to the edge of the Second Woods. Gordon eventually moved his division out of the Second Woods to a stone wall closer to Winchester. Pickens was wounded and Colonel Charles M. Forsyth assumed command of his brigade. Battle ordered a fall back toward Winchester, which began a disorderly retreat.&amp;lt;ref name=&quot;PatchanCh18&quot;/&amp;gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;/td&gt;
